Ministry of Finance's Method for Reducing the Chinese Tea Tax

Order of the Executive Yuan

The Shanghai Special Municipality received Order No. 1251 from the Executive Yuan yesterday, stating: "To inform you, the Municipality previously submitted a report from the Social Affairs Bureau, stating that the Shanghai Tea Industry Association and the Tea Merchants' Guild had repeatedly submitted opinions and requested instructions on methods for reducing or exempting tea taxes. After the report was forwarded to the Ministry of Finance for review and reply, the Ministry replied, stating: 'This case was previously instructed by your Yuan to be handled. Three types of tax reduction methods were drafted and ordered to the National Tariff Commission for investigation and review, and were first submitted for approval. Now, the Commission has replied, stating that implementing Method A is the most effective way to relieve Chinese tea, but changing to a special consumption tax should be premised on central planning and management.' After detailed discussion by the Ministry, it was believed that while reducing or exempting domestic taxes is a temporary solution for relieving Chinese tea, a unified tax law should be formulated for the entire Chinese tea industry to avoid complications that hinder the development of Chinese tea. While under review, the National Government issued an order that all Lijin taxes nationwide would be abolished from October 10, 1930.' The date of implementation is not far off. How domestic Lijin taxes on the transportation and sale of Chinese tea should be reduced or exempted, how export of Chinese tea should be encouraged, and whether special taxes and consumption taxes should be implemented in tea-producing areas of various provinces will undoubtedly be considered with regard to the situation of merchants, the current state of the domestic tea industry, and the trend of international trade, and a comprehensive plan will be carefully formulated and uniformly managed. However, before the national abolition of Lijin taxes is implemented, the old regulations should continue to be followed to avoid confusion. The opinions on reducing or exempting tea taxes submitted by the Shanghai Tea Industry Association and the Shanghai Tea Merchants' Guild, and the opinions on improving Chinese tea formulated by the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau, are undoubtedly adoptable and should be retained as references for revising the tax regulations.' The aforementioned report is hereby ordered to be forwarded to the Municipality for notification."

Extension of the Deadline for Company License Verification

Municipal Government Orders the Bureau to Forward Instructions for Compliance

The Municipal Government issued an order to the Social Affairs and Public Utilities Bureaus yesterday, stating: "To issue an order, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce Commercial Order No. 9225 was approved, stating: 'It has been found that the company's application for verification and renewal of its license was previously extended by the Ministry for six months until December 9 of last year. Subsequently, a further three-month extension was approved by the Executive Yuan and filed for record. The Ministry has issued a bulletin and notified the respective bureaus to follow the instructions. Now that the deadline has expired again, there are still many companies that have not applied for verification within the deadline. The previous registration licenses should have been revoked after investigation. However, due to the impact of military transportation, it is inevitable that the actual verification and renewal cannot be completed in time, so it is not appropriate to revoke them immediately. Therefore, a further extension is granted until September 15 of the third year to show consideration. If the application for verification and renewal is not submitted within the deadline, the licenses issued will be declared invalid. The Ministry has submitted the above to the Executive Yuan for approval and filing. In addition to the public announcement and separate orders, the respective Municipal Governments are requested to investigate and follow the instructions. Furthermore, companies applying for verification and renewal of their licenses should submit the company's articles of association, the latest list of shareholders, and a list of the names and addresses of directors and supervisors for review, and please forward the notification.' The application for verification and renewal of company licenses has been extended for another three months. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce's notification has previously been forwarded for notification. With the approval of the aforementioned information, in addition to separate orders, the respective bureaus are hereby ordered to acknowledge and forward the instructions for compliance."

Assistance in Improving Industrial Goods

Announcement from the Industrial Goods Testing Institute

The China National Products Maintenance Association sent a letter to all members of the National Products Factories yesterday, stating: "We have recently received a letter from the Shanghai Special Municipality Social Affairs Bureau Industrial Goods Testing Institute, stating: 'The decline of our country's industry and commerce is due to many complex reasons, but also because the Chinese people have not fully understood the benefits of science, adhering to outdated methods, producing inferior products, and finding it difficult to compete with imported goods. Regarding the promotion of industrial and commercial scientification in European and American countries, we will not discuss it for now. Even our neighbor, Japan, has made rapid progress in industry and commerce in the past 20 years and has become strong, all by emulating the merits of Europe and America. Currently, there are dozens of industrial research and testing institutions in that country, which solve problems, analyze difficulties, imitate, and improve. On the one hand, it is due to the government's encouragement, but without the manufacturers' knowledge of how to use them, it would be difficult to achieve today's good results. Looking back at our country, although it possesses abundant natural resources, it lacks excellent technology and is subject to economic oppression. The existing factories are closing down every day, and new businesses are as rare as morning stars, which is truly painful to say. In view of this, the Shanghai Municipal Government established the Industrial Testing Institute in its 17-year administrative program, aiming to assist in the improvement of the city's industry and commerce. Any manufacturer in the city who entrusts the Institute with research or testing on technical issues, the Institute is extremely willing to serve. Originally, it was intended to be free of charge, but to avoid unintentional entrustment, a very small handling fee will be charged to show restriction. As for the entrustment of research on improving product or raw material issues, no fees will be charged before the research. The raw materials and supplies required for research can be provided by the entruster or purchased by the Institute. However, a contract must be signed in advance. After the research is successful and effective, the entruster will provide a one-time or annual subsidy to supplement the Institute's funding, so that the Institute's scope can be gradually expanded and its effectiveness can be widespread. This is not only in the interests of both parties. Furthermore, the Institute wants to understand the situation of various industries, so it will send letters to three or four manufacturers every week to discuss in person, so as to understand the technical difficulties of each industry, so as to provide guidance or research and improvement. However, some manufacturers still do not understand the Institute's purpose, and ignore it, neither sending representatives nor responding, which is very regrettable. We have always admired your association as a hub in the business world, and have relied on you to plan for the future of national products in every way. Therefore, we would like to ask your association to widely publicize the Institute's purpose of seeking improvement and development for the city's industry and commerce, so that each manufacturer can understand and utilize it. We hope that you will convey this separately and hope that you will give us your valuable advice.' In light of this, we believe that science is omnipotent, and it is not difficult to test. The progress of goods depends on research and development. The source of wealth and strength lies in this. Now, the Municipal Industrial Goods Testing Institute has made a great vow to serve our country's goods industry and commerce with sincere dedication and determination, which is deeply admired. Moreover, our country's goods manufacturers often lament that they lack the financial resources to conduct research to improve their products and expand sales. Now, there are specialized talents who are willing to do their best, which is what our country's goods industry has been seeking but has not been able to obtain. It is fortunate. Our association sincerely hopes that our manufacturers will develop a close relationship with the Institute and entrust research and improvement with sincerity, so that not only will the factory benefit infinitely, but it will also be the glory of our country's goods industry. This is a special announcement, and we hope that you will investigate and adopt it."

Aftermath of the Reduction of Postal Rates for Overseas Chinese Letters

The National Federation of Commerce sent a telegram to the Ministry of Communications yesterday, stating: "To the Ministry of Communications in Nanjing: On the Geng Day, the Overseas Chinese Congress in Singapore sent a telegram stating: 'To the Shanghai National Chamber of Commerce Federation and the Overseas Chinese Federation: Your association has worked hard to argue for the increased fees for overseas Chinese letters, and all overseas Chinese are grateful. The Singapore general packing method is still followed. The Civil Affairs Bureau is allowed to pack and send the envelopes and affix the total number of stamps outside the package. The number of envelopes is checked against the book, and missing stamps will be punished. This is truly convenient for the people. The Ministry of Communications' Winter Telegram has approved a reduction of 5 cents, and the Shantou, Xiamen, and Shaoxing Bureaus have been ordered to affix the stamps to each envelope before packing, and they also want to change to a special postal agent name. We have telegraphed the Ministry to earnestly order them to follow the old method and not to impose harsh examples on the people. Your association loves and protects overseas Chinese. Please help us.' From Lin Jindian, Singapore Overseas Chinese Congress, and others. The old regulations of packing and sending the envelopes themselves, affixing the total number of stamps outside the package, and checking the number of envelopes against the book, with punishment for missing stamps, are truly convenient for the people. The UK is following the old method, but the Shantou and Xiamen postal bureaus are changing the old regulations, ordering that the stamps be affixed to each envelope before packing, which is time-consuming and inconvenient. We should request a quick telegram to the Shantou and Xiamen postal bureaus to follow the old method. The Civil Affairs Bureau is changing to a special postal agent, but there is no such method in Southeast Asia, and there is no suspicion of violating the Postal Union Convention. Our country does not need to do this, or wait until the Southeast Asian countries implement it before imitating it. We ask for prompt approval and hope for a telegraphic reply.' The National Chamber of Commerce Federation, the Overseas Chinese Federation, etc. Qiyin. In addition, the National Federation of Commerce and the Overseas Chinese Federation have been working hard to argue with the government for the increased postal rates for overseas Chinese letters. Yesterday, the Overseas Chinese Federation received a letter and telegram from the Chaozhou Eight County Chamber of Commerce in Hong Kong and the Chaozhou Beijing Students Association, reporting that the association and other local organizations have joined forces to assist in the case and have sent numerous telegrams to the government to argue for the case, requesting that the old method be followed. The Overseas Chinese Federation immediately replied with thanks and detailed the process of the case and the recent situation."

Overview of the Work of the Drug Workers' Support Association

Since the start of the work of the various labor unions in the Drug Workers' Support Association, the various labor unions have been enthusiastically contacting and assisting the drug workers, and sending representatives to comfort them. Since the strike began, almost a month has passed. Although they are suffering from hunger and cold, their attitude of indignation has not diminished. They are determined not to resume work until their goal is achieved. The fundraising team sent by the support association, in addition to going to Zhabei, Nanshi, Pudong and other places to solicit donations from various labor unions, also worked with the propaganda and communication departments to give speeches to various labor unions about the negotiation process between the drug industry labor and management, and they all helped generously. This shows one aspect of the hard work of the support association.

The Association of Families of the May 30th Victims Held a Regular Meeting Yesterday

The Association of Families of the Martyrs of the Shanghai May 30th Massacre, after receiving the compensation from the Municipal Council, distributed the first batch of compensation to the registered family members and injured comrades on the same day. On March 12th, the second batch of compensation was distributed to the registered and verified family members and injured comrades. Yesterday, the association called a meeting of all family members who had received compensation to discuss solutions because there were still more than 20 family members and injured persons who had not registered with the association, or because their addresses were unknown, or because they had moved to other places, making it impossible to notify them. More than 20 people attended, and Hu Chang-sheng was elected as chairman, Chen Fu-cai as master of ceremonies, and Pan Qian-chu as recorder. The meeting included (1) Reporting matters: (A) The chairman reported the purpose of the meeting, (B) Chen Fu-cai reported the organizational process of the association and the two distributions of compensation, (C) The chairman reported that there were still unregistered family members, stating that the association would close on June 30th. However, there are still four families, Yin Jing-yi, Chen Xing-fa, Chen Yu-qin, and Xu Luo-feng, and seventeen injured persons, Shen A-qi, Xu Rui-he, Wei Chun-ting, Chen Yun-qiu, Chen Jin-fa, Cai Hong-chun, Wang You-yi, Yu Mao-huai, Wang Ru-ping, Liu Shao-xian, Yu Guan-zhu, Ma Mi-jun, Zhou Ren-lian, Mei He-shang, Li Yi-xun, Chen Bao-cong, and Mei Zhong-lin, whose addresses are unknown or who have moved to other places, making it impossible for the association to notify them, and the family members do not know about the association. No leniency will be given if there is no evidence. (B) The names of the 21 family members, Yin Jing-yi, etc., who will register in the future will be announced in the report. (Resolution) Passed. (C) What should be done if they still do not come to register by the deadline? (Resolution) The compensation that is due will be transferred to the board of directors of the May 30th Cemetery for safekeeping as a cemetery fund. (D) Should the deadline be extended or prolonged? (Resolution) June 30th will be the deadline, and there will be no further extensions or prolongations. If they do not come to register by the deadline, it will be considered that they have voluntarily given up their rights. (3) Temporary motions (A) The chairman proposed that Li Yu-shu came to the meeting to represent Hu Pei-liang, Wang Xiao-long, Zhou A-da, Wang Fu, Dong A-si, Pan Xiao-yunzi, and Xu A-bing, who were shot or beaten with sticks in Xiaosha Ferry, to register. After careful investigation by the association, the blood case records did not have the names of Hu and seven others, and the board of directors did not have a report or confirmation of Hu's disaster at that time. What should be done? (Resolution) Not accepted. (B) The chairman proposed that the association has been established for more than four years. Although the compensation negotiations have been resolved and the government will continue to negotiate the compensation part, the association plans to keep a commemorative publication to record the immortality. Please vote on the proposal. (Resolution) Approve the publication of the association's commemorative publication, and record the events since the establishment of the association on the commemorative publication. The portraits of the bereaved families and injured comrades must also be attached to the commemorative publication. Hu and Chen were re-elected to preside over the matter. The meeting adjourned, and it was already late at night.

This is the most severely affected area. The disaster victims are all using wild grass and bark to fill their stomachs, and some are even starving to death. The situation is truly unbearable to witness. They escaped in winter and returned in spring, but the farmers have no food to eat, no seeds to plant, and no strength to cultivate. The suffering is especially severe. Our chairman and the gentlemen are kind and compassionate, with the aim of saving people and thoroughly helping them. Shu-lun respectfully followed the strict investigation and heavy release, removing the households with minor disasters. However, there are too many serious disasters, and it is impossible to remove them all. The spring relief this year is widespread and the funds are low, which is useless. We can only ask for additional funds in order to evenly distribute the kindness and avoid omissions. Public Security Bureau Pays Attention to Refugees Passing Through

The Shanghai Special Municipal Public Security Bureau issued an order to all district offices yesterday, stating that the city has convenient transportation. Based on the number of refugees passing through the city last year, there were more than 6,000 people. Now that the busy farming season is coming, there will be quite a few returning to their hometowns to farm. We are deeply concerned that unscrupulous people will pretend to be refugees and try to disturb the local area. It is not enough to eliminate hidden dangers without strict prevention at all times. In addition to the separate orders, the order is to instruct the heads of each district office to follow the instructions, order their subordinates to pay attention at all times, and when refugees pass through, in addition to taking care of and suppressing them, they should also carefully monitor them. If there are people with suspicious behavior, they should immediately report them for verification and handling. This order.

When Will the China Merchants Bureau Dispute End?

Li Gu-fan Sues Li Guo-jie Again

Raises Four Points of Accusation

Recently, lawsuits involving the China Merchants Bureau have emerged one after another. First, there was the criminal mutual accusation between Zhao Tie-qiao, the General Manager of the bureau, and Li Guo-jie, the Chairman of the board of directors and Manager of the Jiyu Company. Then, Zhao, the General Manager, appointed Fu Ju-cun, the Manager of the Jiyu Company, to sue Li Guo-jie for refusing to hand over the managerial position. Now, Li Gu-fan, a shareholder of the bureau, has sued Li Guo-jie and Ou Tang-rong for illegally holding a meeting. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Cheng Shang-qing of the Special District Court opened a trial. First, the plaintiff stated the reasons (1) At the meeting held on February 22nd and 23rd of this year, the shareholders present did not reach more than half of the total number of shareholders. The company has more than 40,000 shares, and only 15,000 shares were present on that day. (2) The restriction on equity violates the Company Law. (3) The Jiyu Company is an agency of the China Merchants Bureau. The shareholders' meeting of the Jiyu Company should be convened by the China Merchants Bureau. It is illegal to convene it by the Jiyu Company. (4) The registration of the Jiyu Company is illegal. Based on the above reasons, I filed the lawsuit. Then, Li's lawyer added that the China Merchants Bureau and the Jiyu Company are closely related. The property of the China Merchants Bureau is managed by the Jiyu Company. If the two are separated, the collateral on which the bureau relies to borrow money will be gone. Neither of the defendants was present, and their representative lawyers replied that the four reasons stated by the plaintiff were as follows: (1) Although the number of people present at the meeting was not enough for the quorum, all the resolutions complied with the company's regulations. They were treated as provisional resolutions and passed at the second meeting before becoming resolutions. However, due to the lawsuit, the meeting has not yet been held. (2) The regulations on the shareholding system are in accordance with the Company Law. (3) The Jiyu Company applied to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for registration in February of the 18th year and was approved and issued a license. It can be separated from the China Merchants Bureau. (4) The registration is of course legal. As for the plaintiff's lawyer saying that the China Merchants Bureau must rely on the company, it is also inaccurate. The capital of the China Merchants Bureau is 8 million yuan, and although the debt is 14 million yuan, its assets are still worth 40 million yuan. How can it lead to bankruptcy? Judge Cheng stated that it is questionable whether this case should be resolved by the administrative organ or handled by the judicial office. He should wait for consideration and handling, and then adjourn the hearing to another date.

Lawyer States Divorce Request is Extremely Firm

Vows Not to Return Home Until Goal is Achieved

Ms. Fang Also Did Not Appear in Court Yesterday

Official Urges Both Parties to Reconcile

Ms. Fang Wen-xian, the sister of wealthy businessman Fang Jiao-bo, has been married to the famous jockey Hu Hui-lin for 16 years. After Hu fell in love with Mina, the eldest daughter of illusionist Lang De-shan, he disregarded his children and abandoned his wife. Recently, he hired a lawyer to file for divorce from his wife, as reported in the previous newspaper. The case was tried by Judge Cheng Shang-feng of the Special District Court at 2:30 PM yesterday. Neither the plaintiff nor the defendant appeared in person, and each appointed a lawyer to represent them. First, the plaintiff's lawyer said that Hu Hui-lin is now in London, England, so he could not appear in court. He and Ms. Fang have been married for more than ten years and have seven children, but their relationship has not been harmonious and they often quarreled while living together. Hu is skilled in horse riding and has won many awards. These awards are obtained in exchange for Hu's reputation, which cannot be obtained with money. His wife sold these awards, which Hu was most saddened by. Therefore, this time he requested a divorce extremely firmly. Hu once said that if he cannot achieve the goal of divorce, he will vow not to return home. The defendant's lawyer also said that the defendant, Fang Wen-xian, knew that her husband was named Hu Hui-lin and was now in the United States. Now reading the complaint, it is written as Hu Hui-lin, and the plaintiff's lawyer also said that he is now in England. It is still questionable whether this person is the defendant's husband. Since he is in England, why is the cross in the complaint signed by the plaintiff himself? It is difficult to explain. The plaintiff's lawyer immediately replied that the plaintiff's name is an English name, and Hui and Hui are translated incorrectly. The cross in the complaint was signed by our lawyer. Under the debate between the lawyers of both sides, Judge Cheng instructed the lawyers of both sides to go out and inform the parties to reconcile, so as to avoid litigation. The lawyers then retreated.

The Case is Quite Bizarre

The Deceased Was Shot in the Forehead

Said to Have Been Playing with a Gun

The Court Will Examine Today

Zhang Tian-xing, a Suzhou native living at No. 22 Delan Roomfang, Shipinoung, in the city, was engaged to Wang Xiao-mei, and their marriage was approaching. Unexpectedly, an accident occurred yesterday morning, and the unmarried woman died unjustly, which is also a painful event in life. However, as the matter is extraordinary, there are many disputes, and the court is scheduled to examine the case this morning. How did it happen? The truth will be revealed soon. The incident occurred before noon yesterday. After the public security bureau of the first office of the second district heard the news, the director and patrol officers went to investigate. They learned that Zhang Tian-xing was wiping the pistol he was wearing in the pavilion room on the second floor around 11:30 AM yesterday, facing the window and facing away from the door. Zhang said that after he finished wiping, he was afraid that the bullets in the gun clip would cause a mistake when using it, so he inserted the magazine to try to pull it. Who knew that his unmarried woman, Wang Xiao-mei, suddenly came to his side and pulled him, accidentally touching the firing pin, and the bullet flew out, hitting her forehead. She fell to the ground at that time and died before she could be treated. The police investigation revealed that there were six bullets remaining in the clip. The gun was a Browning type, with words such as "Hu Shu Yi Si Qi Jiu" on it. The deceased was 24 years old and was the sister of Wang Pin-xiang from Nanxiang. After the engagement, the relationship was still good. She came to Shanghai the day before yesterday and lived in Zhang Tian-xing's house. They were going to be married on the 24th of this month. After the deceased was shot, she was lying on the ground, and the situation was extremely tragic. The bullet entered from the brow and remained in her head, causing a bulge in the back of her head. According to Zhang, his brother Jin-fu was writing in the room when the accident occurred. The layout of the room where the accident occurred is roughly as follows: a table is placed on the right side of the window, and the bed is on the left side. The door to enter and exit is opposite the bed. Zhang's brother opened Zhang Hexing Paint Shop, and the downstairs of his residence is rented as a clothing store. It is said that the deceased Wang Xiao-mei came from downstairs after seeing the wedding clothes before the accident. Alas.

Medical Treatment Was Ineffective and She Died

The Poor Old Mother Spurted Blood Upon Hearing the News

Cantonese prostitute Luo Huizhu and her fellow villager Guo Jinhua were deeply in love and vowed to marry each other. Unexpectedly, Guo was short of money and had no resources to marry Luo. Since the prostitute entered the hospital, she believed that her lover had died for her, so why could she live alone? Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities Punishes Well-Drilling Company for Illegal Business Operations

The Tianhe Well Drilling Company on Bubbling Well Road in this city has not registered with the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities and is operating without a license. The Engineering Society Holds a Farewell Dinner for Huang Boqiao and Others

On the 7th of this month at 7 PM, the Chinese Engineering Society held a public farewell dinner for Huang Boqiao, Wang Shengshen, and Wu Jian (Mr. Wu is still in Hankou), representatives attending the Second World Power Conference in Berlin. Guests included Zhu Kezhen, President of the Science Society of China, Chen Guojun, Deputy Secretary-General of the China Construction Association, Yang Junsheng, representative of the Chinese Society for the Advancement of Learning, and Li Yanshi, who is attending the Power Conference independently. Members present included Xu Peihuang, Guo Chengen, Shen Yi, Xue Cixin, Li Keng, Wang Bailei, Li Chu, Yang Xiliu, Huang Bingkui, Wang Xingxin, Zhu Shuyi, Tan Boyu, and over sixty others. The chairman, Hu Shuhua, presided. During the dinner, Chairman Hu rose and gave a speech, stating that considering the size of China, it was regrettable that only three or four people were attending the Second World Power Conference, which was less than other countries. However, no one from China participated in the First Power Conference held in London in 1924. Although the number is small this time, the quality is excellent. Germany has recovered since the European War and its industrial progress is particularly remarkable. Moreover, its political aspect no longer has the color of imperialism. Industrial talents are especially willing to connect with our country. With these conveniences, it is certain that each representative will return with great contributions to the motherland after the conference. Zhu Kezhen, Chen Guojun, Yang Junsheng, and others then delivered farewell speeches, offering much encouragement. Xue Cixin, Vice President of the Shanghai Branch, and members Guo Chengen, Tan Boyu, and others also spoke. Mr. Huang Boqiao and Mr. Li Jiashi gave speeches in reply. Mr. Huang also said that this time, our country's attendance was small, the funding was insufficient, and there was no contribution in terms of power, deeply regretting the unimpressive appearance. Mr. Hu then stated that the material civilization of Europe and America was comparable to that of our country before James Watt completed the steam engine, which was only about one hundred and seventy years ago. If we strive to be strong, who knows whether we will not rival Europe and America in a hundred years? He asked Mr. Huang not to be discouraged and raised a glass to wish him a smooth journey. The gathering ended in joy at 10 PM.

The Case of the American Ship Crashing into a Stone Boat

Refusing to Pay Compensation

The American merchant ship *Voluntian*, belonging to Foreland Company, recently arrived in Shanghai from the United States carrying cargo. While sailing on the Huangpu River in front of the Tongxing Cotton Mill, it collided with the *Jin Jia Zhen*, a stone-carrying boat which failed to give way in time. The *Jin Jia Zhen* was broken in two by the collision. Fortunately, no one was injured. Afterwards, the ship owner, along with the Stone Guild and the Ningbo Fellow-Villagers Association, negotiated with the company for compensation. Foreland Company hired an appraiser, Maiton, to investigate the accident site. It is now reported that one section of the sunken boat was stolen, and the other section is still on the river surface. The investigation concluded that the American ship was sailing on its designated route and made no mistake, making it difficult to assign responsibility for compensation. A letter of attestation was also obtained from the captain of a certain warship stationed there. Yesterday, this decision was communicated in a letter to the Ningbo Fellow-Villagers Association, expressing their refusal to pay compensation.

Does Not Wish to Return with Her Mother

Yang Shannan was accused by Suzhou woman Wu He of hiding her daughter. Yesterday afternoon, Zhou, a judge of the Special District Court, convened a hearing. According to the plaintiff, her daughter, Cui Bao, 20 years old, was pawned by her husband five years ago to the defendant's brothel to work as a servant. At that time, she was in Beiping. Later, she learned that her daughter had been lured into prostitution and had given birth to two children. After coming to Shanghai, she negotiated with the defendant to take her back, but the defendant hid Cui Bao. Therefore, she is suing, asking the court to order the return of her daughter and to pay her 4,000 yuan as child support for her daughter's two children. According to the defendant's statement, Cui Bao was pawned to my brothel, and she gave birth to children with customers of her own free will. Later, Cui Bao hired a lawyer to dissolve the relationship with me, and she left with the lawyer. I do not know her whereabouts. Wu Cui Bao also hired a lawyer to participate in the case, requesting permission to end the mother-daughter relationship with Wu He. According to Cui Bao's statement, "I entered the brothel because my mother pawned me. Later, I shaved my head and gave birth to children of my own free will. It was not forced by the defendant. Now I am married to He Yueqi and will not return with my mother." After the lawyers for both parties presented their arguments, Judge Zhou declared the debate closed and scheduled a date for the verdict.

The Woman at the Scene of the Lunatic's Murder Case Was Summoned Yesterday

In the case of the lunatic Zhang Jiazhen killing a woman and a child on Zhonghua Road in Xiaonanmen, Yang, the investigating officer of the District Court, summoned He Jiumei, the woman who was nearly killed at the time, to the case for questioning yesterday. According to her statement, she is 21 years old and lives in Xiaonanmen. At 1 PM at the end of last month, she and the deceased Wu Zhou went to work at a sock factory. While walking to the entrance of Tianfu Lane on Zhonghua Road, she didn't know where the lunatic came from. Later, she saw the deceased rush forward, and when she turned her head, she saw the murderer holding a knife, and had already stabbed Wu Zhou's head and neck. Surprised, she asked what was happening, and then the murderer grabbed me. I struggled and escaped and haven't dared to go out since. I didn't know what happened afterwards, but we didn't know the murderer at all. The officer ordered her to return home and wait for further instructions.

Rickshaw Puller Ambushed in the Dark

Three Thugs Arrive Suddenly

The Rickshaw Puller's Life is in Grave Danger

At around 8:45 PM last night, Xu Xiaozhang, a former rickshaw puller, was walking along Tangshan Road on Yunli Lane in Hongkou. Three people wearing blue cloth shirts and pants suddenly emerged from the darkness. Without any explanation, they produced a handgun and fired three shots at Xu's head, two shots at his right leg, and one shot at his left hand. Blood gushed out, and he fell to the ground. The assailants disappeared without a trace. A Western police officer, number 107, from the Wayside Police Station, patrolling the area, sent the injured rickshaw puller to Tongren Hospital for treatment. However, Xu was unable to speak when he arrived at the hospital and died several minutes later.

A Monk Does Not Abide by Monastic Rules

Spending a Night Out

Resulting in Three Days of Detention

Yuanzhao, a monk residing at Longhua Temple, recently discovered that his disciple Guangwen did not abide by the rules and spent the night outside. After repeated warnings failed, he handed Guangwen over to the Sixth District, Third Precinct. Chief Liu briefly questioned him. Guangwen stated that his Dharma name was Guangwen, he was from Shandong, and was 24 years old. He had been a monk since he was young. The previous day, a fellow villager visited him, and they went to see a play in Shanghai. It was inconvenient to return at night, so he stayed overnight in a hotel. He returned the next day and there was no misconduct. Chief Liu ordered the monk to be detained for three days as a warning for unauthorized absence and disobedience to his teacher.

Another Woman Arrested in the Case of the Four Banks' Reserve Robbery

Accused of Relaying Stolen Money for the Bandits

Several bandits involved in the armed robbery of the Four Banks' Reserve have been successively arrested by the police. The day before yesterday, detectives from the Municipal Public Security Bureau also arrested Zhao Wang, a woman from Suzhou, at No. 1, Qinglian Road, Nanshi, who was related to the case. The Zhabei Police Station learned of this and transferred Zhao Wang back to their station. Yesterday, they were sent to the Special District Court for questioning. According to Detective Liang Chengyu, Zhao Wang confessed to the Public Security Bureau that she had relayed stolen money from Yuan Genfa to a certain woman. Judge Zhou questioned her briefly and ordered the defendant to be detained, with the case to be tried jointly with the other defendants at a later date.

False Receipts Used to Collect Match Account Payments

Is It Acceptable to Do It Again?

Caught After Second Attempt

The Lao Shen Da Tobacco and Paper Shop in Zhongshi Town, Caojiadu, Huxi, has been open for many years and its business is quite prosperous. It sells matches and purchases them from the Baochang Match Company on Pingjili Road in the French Concession. Payments are made regularly on settlement days. However, last month, Fei Jiqing, an employee of the Huichang Company, an agency of the match company, fabricated a receipt from the match company and forged a letter of authorization (the letter stated that the match company had authorized him to collect payment). He went to the Shen Da Shop to collect payment. The shop believed it was genuine and paid the amount of over one hundred and ten yuan in full. Later, the shop purchased two more cases of matches from the company, but neither side mentioned the previous payment. On the 5th of this month, Fei Jiqing again used a false receipt to collect payment for one case of matches. The shop stated that they had purchased two cases, so why was he only collecting payment for one case? Fei immediately said that it must have been a mistake by the accountant and promised to check and return later. The wheels of justice turn slowly, but grind finely. The next day (the 6th), Du Shaoquan, a salesman from the match company, arrived at the shop with a formal receipt to collect both new and old accounts. The shop then realized that Fei had fraudulently collected the payment and told Du about the situation. On the afternoon of the 7th, Fei still dared to go to the shop with a false receipt for two cases of matches and demanded payment. The shop stallled him and immediately reported it to the match company by telephone. The match company sent representatives who stated that they had verified that Fei had fraudulently collected over one thousand yuan from various places. They took Fei Jiqing, along with the forged letter and receipts, to the headquarters of the Fourth Team of the Thirteenth Branch of the Songhu Security Group in the town. The team sent a letter to the Sixth District Police Station for investigation. Fei Jiqing confessed that he was 27 years old, a local, and worked at the Huichang Company, admitting that he had fraudulently collected payment from the shop. The manager of the Huichang Company also surrendered himself, requesting that Fei be punished according to the law. Yesterday, a document was prepared and sent to the District Court for investigation.

The Fourth District Detective Team Cracks a Robbery and Murder Case

Leading to the Resolution of Multiple Cases

The Detective Team of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau in Zhabei recently solved a robbery and murder case, along with cracking the case of a patrolman being killed in the Public Concession and other theft cases. In investigating the robbery and murder case at the Jufeng Charcoal Shop on Xiexu Road, on the 4th, they received a tip that Chen Bilu, a known bandit, was involved in the case and was hiding at No. 719, Xiejiayu Lane, Ximalu, Jing'an Temple Road. Led by Public Security Officer Liu Shaoda and Detective Shi Yunling of the Detective Team of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau, they went to the address along with detectives from the patrol force. Chen Bilu was not at home, but three handguns, thirty bullets, a Mauser pistol, and eight bullets were found in the bed. Chen's wife, Cao, was also taken to the police station. Later, according to a tip, the fugitive Gu Cailin had enticed a young woman and was hiding in Room 25 of a certain hotel in the concession. Officer Xia led detectives to arrest Chen. He confessed to robbing the charcoal shop on Xiexu Road with Wang Dalu, Lu Ancheng, and Xu Liu. Wang Dalu shot and killed a man outside the door. They also repeatedly robbed the Shixing Guild Hall in Nanshi and a Wang family's house in Che Yang Fangzi Lane. However, regarding the shooting of the patrolman behind the Yong'an Cotton Mill in the Public Concession, he said that he was not involved. When the detectives were searching Chen Bilu's house, they sent detectives to guard it and subsequently arrested the bandits Yu Jinshan, Dai Lixuan, and Li Desheng. They confessed to robbing the Tianfuli on Meiyuan Road, the Gujiawan Glass Factory, the north side of the railroad's Caozha, and a thatched shed at the end of Datong Road with others. The bandits have been sent by the Fourth District Public Security Bureau to the Judicial Section for review.

Russians Arrested for Robbery at the Station

Two Russians, Sanbaideng Lifu and another, along with one fugitive, were first caught pickpocketing at the Beijing-Shanghai Railway North Station at 9 AM. When passengers saw this, they tried to stop them, but the Russians became reckless and started robbing them. The passengers shouted for help from the police who arrived and arrested the two Russians, while one escaped. They were immediately escorted to the Police Department and transferred to the District Court for punishment yesterday.

Detective Team Cracks Theft Case

Zhang Guizhen's house at No. 16, Zhangjiazhai, Hongzhen, was suddenly robbed on the 3rd of this month. Six robbers came, two of them holding handguns. They robbed five or six gold rings, two gold watches, gold earrings, clothes, etc., and left with a whoop. Afterwards, detectives arrested Chen Yangzhi, a 32-year-old native of Qingjiang, at the Hanzhao Intersection of Xinmin Road in Zhabei on the afternoon of the previous day. He lived in a bungalow behind the racecourse on Yangshupu Road and had previously served as a soldier in Jiangbei.

Briton Fined for Traffic Violation

Jeffcott Fined Five Pounds

The *Wenhui Bao* reports that Jeffcott, a British chemical assistant at the Shanghai Electric Power Company, drove his car drunk on the afternoon of March 29th, driving erratically on Sichuan Road. Later, at the corner of Ningbo Road, he overturned a rickshaw. He ignored the order of the Chinese police to stop and drove into Ningbo Road, hitting a small car. Near Tianjin, the Chinese police, with the help of an Indian police officer, finally dragged Jeffcott out of the car and sent him to the General Police Station by rickshaw. This morning (the 8th), the British Consular Court opened the trial. The Chinese and Indian police officers present testified to everything. The defendant admitted to the violation. The presiding officer Anderson fined him five British pounds, equivalent to seventy-three yuan and eight jiao in Shanghai silver currency, and gave him a warning, saying that he was lucky that he did not cause a major disaster that day, otherwise, the fine would not have been the only punishment.

Verdict in the Rui Xiang Abuse Case

The Mother Sentenced to Two Months Imprisonment, Suspended

The Daughter Sentenced to Two Months Imprisonment

The Hangzhou woman Chen Tang, residing at No. 371 and a half, Defu Lane, Mahuo Road, and her married daughter Yan Chen jointly abused their 11-year-old maid Rui Xiang. Detectives Liang Baosheng and Zhou Guisheng of the Xinzha Police Station arrested the two women and brought them to the former Provisional Court for questioning. This was reported previously. Yesterday morning, Judge Sun Yuan of the Special District Court opened a hearing to continue the trial. Shen Chen, a witness woman, was brought to court to testify to the cruel behavior of the defendant mother and daughter in abusing the maid. Judge Sun questioned the two defendants and Rui Xiang. Then, Bao Yi, the lawyer from the patrol force, began the debate, requesting strict punishment to uphold humanity. Judge Sun then announced the verdict: Chen Tang was sentenced to two months imprisonment for joint assault, suspended for two years. Yan Chen was sentenced to two months imprisonment. Rui Xiang was sent to Jiliang Institute for care.

Anti-Opium Society Releases Shocking Statistics

Over Fourteen Million Taels of Persian Opium Exported Last Year

The International Section and Investigation Section of the China National Anti-Opium Society recently conducted a detailed investigation into the import of Persian opium (commonly known as red soil) into China, which has poisoned society and caused endless harm. According to their statistics, from December 17th to the end of November 18th, over four hundred and eleven tons of opium were shipped from the two ports of Bosseia and Mohammilla in Persia, totaling fourteen million seven hundred and thirty thousand two hundred and forty taels. The exports by country are approximately as follows: (Russia) Vladivostok, 2,320 boxes, 5,551,680 taels; (UK) Singapore, 2,079 boxes, 4,677,120 taels; (China) Dalian, 764 boxes, 1,953,280 taels; (Portugal) Macau, 400 boxes, 1,021,440 taels; (Japan) Keelung, 350 boxes, 809,600 taels; (Germany) Hamburg, 240 boxes, 624,800 taels; (Siam) Bangkok, 200 boxes, 448,000 taels; (Netherlands) Batavia, 100 boxes, 258,800 taels; (USA) New York, 70 boxes, 117,120 taels; (UK) Sandakan, 50 boxes, 197,120 taels. The total export amount reached 6,573 boxes. Among them, 4,063 boxes were exported by British ships, 1,908 boxes were exported by Chinese ships, 412 boxes were exported by Japanese ships, and 190 boxes were exported by German ships. The 2,320 boxes exported from Persia to Vladivostok were actually never arrived at the port. They were completely smuggled into China and the bulk was smuggled into Shanghai and sold to various places. In addition, the Persian opium imported from Batavia, Singapore, Dalian, Keelung, Macau, Sandakan, and Bangkok is entirely used by the local colonial governments to poison our overseas Chinese. The numbers exported to New York and Hamburg are for the manufacture of narcotic drugs.

The above opium, calculated at the Shanghai opium market price, is worth about 60 million yuan. Our people are impoverished and exhausted, and yet they bear this additional burden to buy poisons that harm their bodies and exterminate their race. Is this not a great calamity for our country? It is hoped that the people of the country will rise up together to reject opium and eliminate this poison that destroys the country and exterminates our race.

Selecting Locations for Public Housing

The *New Shanghai News* reports that the number of shanties in Shanghai, according to the Public Security Bureau's statistics from 1928, is approximately 10,975 households in Nanshi, 2,336 households in Huxi, and 415 households in Wusong. However, there has been an inevitable increase in the past year, and the total number should be in the tens of thousands of households. As a result, whenever a fire occurs, dozens of families are burned, and their hunger and suffering are truly miserable. Therefore, the construction of public housing is a matter of utmost urgency. Recognizing this, the Municipal Government invited various charitable organizations in Shanghai to form a committee for planning and constructing public housing. After its establishment, the committee constructed over one hundred public housing units and an assembly hall in the Quanjia'an Road, Zhabei. It also surveyed the vacant land of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway Bureau at the intersection of Xietu Road and Luban Road in Nanshi as the site for the second public housing project and has reported it to the Municipal Government for the record. As for the construction of housing in other districts of the city, the appropriate locations should be selected in each district based on the number of shanties and the need for housing in the area for future sequential development. However, the Zhabei area is vast and the shanties are scattered, accounting for nearly one-half of the total number of shanties in the city. The one location on Quanjia'an Road is not enough to meet the needs of the western districts in the area. It seems that it should be divided into two locations. As for the four locations in Huxi, Nanshi, Pudong, and Wusong, one housing project is planned for construction in each area, so that when sufficient funds are raised in the future, they can be constructed sequentially. Therefore, the plan for the construction locations in each district has been resolved by the 30th Standing Committee Meeting of the Public Housing Construction Committee. However, due to the difficulty in raising funds, the realization of construction is still far away.

Japanese Car Collides with Public Bus

Yesterday afternoon around 1:35 PM, Public Bus No. 121, registration No. 5815, belonging to the Public Bus Company of the Public Concession and running from Caojiadu to Gaolang Bridge on Bazilu, was traveling from Caojiadu when a car, owned by the Japanese merchant Morimura Car Company, Concession License No. 3575, Municipal Government License No. 925, was speeding towards it from the opposite direction at the Dongzhuan Wan of Wujiaochang. Due to the driver's carelessness, it crashed directly into the front of the public bus. Although the brakes were applied, the front of the public bus was damaged. The police officer on duty saw this and detained both the driver of the car, Du Juyuan, and the driver of the public bus, at the Sixth District Police Station for investigation.

The Arrest for Conspiracy to Steal Rickshaws

Six Jiangbei natives, Bian Xiaorenzi, Lü Lugui, Tan Xiaofuzi, Guo Xiaowuzi, Xie Xiaosizi, and Shen Guirong, conspired to steal several rickshaws from the rickshaw companies opened by Zhang Faji and Peng Yuzhi in the French Concession some days ago. They hid the stolen vehicles at Weng Changgen's house, intending to sell them off. The crime was discovered by French Concession detectives Qin Youyu and Xu Guilin, who arrested the seven individuals, recovered the stolen goods, and brought them to the police station. Yesterday, they were brought to the French Court for prosecution. First, the plaintiffs filed complaints about the theft. When questioned, Bian Xiaorenzi and the others confessed to the conspiracy to steal. Weng Changgen confessed that Bian and the others hid the stolen vehicles at his place, agreeing to pay him one yuan per vehicle per day, which was true. Judge Zhu sentenced Bian to three months in the Western Jail, Lü and Tan to two months each, Guo and the other three to six weeks each, and Weng to a fine of five yuan, or five days in jail as a warning.

Assault Without Cause Settled with Fine

Yang Erxi, residing on Route Kahn in the French New Concession, was assaulted by Cui Wansun, a Jiangbei native, who came with Zhu Pinsan and others to seize and beat him a few days ago. Detectives and patrolmen arrived and arrested Cui and Zhu, bringing them to the police station. Yesterday, they were brought to the French Court for prosecution. The plaintiff, Yang Erxi, stated that the defendant, Cui Wansun, had barged into his house for no reason, asking for someone without saying who. This led to a minor argument. Unexpectedly, Cui returned with several people shortly after and, without asking why, seized and beat him. Fortunately, detectives arrived and made the arrest. He requested severe punishment. Cui Wansun confessed that he went to the plaintiff's house to look for a friend but couldn't find him. When the plaintiff punched him, he became enraged and invited friends to reason with him. He stammered in his testimony. Zhu Pinsan testified that he was there to mediate and did not participate in the assault. Judge Zhu fined Cui fifteen yuan, or fifteen days in jail if he couldn't pay. Zhu was fined ten yuan, or ten days in jail if he couldn't pay, as a warning.

Lost Mute Girl Awaiting Claim

The Municipal Public Security Bureau reported yesterday that a lost mute girl had been sent in by the First Precinct, First Station. Efforts were made to inquire, but she only communicated through gestures. She appeared to be 24 years old and had children at home. For unknown reasons, she was beaten by an old man, left in anger, and got lost. The mute girl has a long face, her hair has been cut off, and she wears a brass headband. She is dressed in a black cloth vest with blue buttons, a blue cloth jacket with white stripes, a black cotton-padded coat, a blue striped white undershirt, blue cloth trousers, black socks, and black shoes. The mute girl has been temporarily sent to the New General Orphanage to be cared for and await her family.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the Shandong coast is clear, the Yangtze River basin and the southern coast are cloudy with occasional rain and fog, the weather is bad over the Yellow Sea and East China Sea with cyclones, the winds in the Bohai Sea and the Taiwan Strait are erratic, and the temperature in Shanghai within 24 hours before 3 PM yesterday was 61.7 degrees at its highest and 55.3 degrees at its lowest, while the highest and lowest temperatures on the same day last year were 70.9 degrees and 47.3 degrees respectively.

Letter Received

To the editor, I am writing to you regarding the article in today's newspaper about the German Minister's arrival in Shanghai on the 10th. Some of the details are not entirely accurate. According to our understanding, the Minister's trip from Pingnan to China is to go to the capital to discuss several official matters. Therefore, he arrived in Shanghai and proceeded to Beijing on the morning of the 11th. He also plans to meet with the German industrial delegation in Beijing at the same time. We are writing this letter specifically to ask your newspaper to make the necessary corrections. Respectfully submitted to the Shen Bao Editorial Office, The German Consulate, April 8th.

Complete Plan for the National Education Conference (2)

(6) Budget for Compulsory Education Expenses

Public financial management should be based on the principle of allocating funds according to resources. This is a fiscal issue, and a separate financial plan should be formulated by the financial authorities after the education plan is determined. A preliminary budget for compulsory education expenditures for the next twenty years is hereby proposed as follows:

Budget Table for Achieving Four Years of Compulsory Education Nationwide in Twenty Years

Budget

Item　Startup Costs Recurring Costs Total

Year 1　National Compulsory Education College　$1,000,000　$200,000 Central Compulsory Education Experimental Zone　$50,000　$28,000　$1,278,000

(Note) The Central Compulsory Education Experimental Zone is based on a standard of 100 teachers for 4,000 children, with a startup cost of $500 per class and an expense of $7 per student.

Year 2　Continuation of Year 1 Projects　$228,000 Provincial/Special Municipality/Rural Normal Colleges and Advanced Courses (30 schools)　$6,000,000　$3,000,000 Provincial Compulsory Education Experimental Zones (60 locations)　$1,500,000　$840,000　$11,568,000

(Note) Each rural normal college and advanced course has a startup cost of $200,000 and recurring costs of $100,000. The startup cost per class and expense per student in the provincial and municipal compulsory education experimental zones are the same as above.

Currently, the financial authorities have not clearly delineated the provincial tax and local municipal and county taxes. Therefore, it is difficult to have precise estimates for the method of sharing compulsory education expenses between the province and the counties and cities. Assuming that the central government and the province each bear half in the second year, starting from the third year, the central government will bear 45% of the compulsory education expenses, the province will bear 10%, and the local governments will bear 45%. Efforts should also be made to encourage private schools to reduce the public burden.

Notes

(Note 1) The so-called "school attendance period" refers to situations such as wheat harvest breaks or half-day schools.

(Note 2) Currently, the national treasury is empty, there is a shortage of teachers, and rural farmers need children to help with work. If all school-age children nationwide are to enroll in school for four years without interruption, it may be difficult to achieve in reality. Therefore, a flexible approach is proposed, where children subject to compulsory education can choose one of the following five enrollment methods based on their family circumstances: A. Enroll in a formal primary school for four years.

B. Enroll in a formal primary school for three years, then switch to a supplementary school, studying for two hours every evening. After completing two years, it can be considered as graduation from elementary school. C. Enroll in a formal primary school for two years, then switch to a supplementary school, studying for two hours every evening. After completing four years, it can also be considered as graduation from elementary school.

D. Enroll in a formal primary school for one year, then switch to a supplementary school, studying for two hours every evening. After completing six years, it can also be considered as graduation from elementary school.

E. Those who cannot attend formal primary school continuously for one year or less can attend school for half a year each year. After two years, they can then enter a supplementary school to complete their elementary education.

In summary, one year of formal primary school is equivalent to two years of supplementary education, and half a year of formal primary school is equivalent to one year of supplementary education. Those who cannot continue attending formal primary school must enter a supplementary school to complete their required education. However, school-age children must attend formal primary school for at least one year, either continuously or divided into two half-year sessions.

(Note 3) These supplementary schools are specifically designed for children who cannot attend formal primary school. The content of the courses taught is the same as that of elementary school, but the curriculum of one year is taught over two years. In addition to two hours of classes every evening, students must be assigned homework to complete at home to compensate for the lack of classroom work.

(Note 4) The so-called self-study system involves assigning the required courses to children for self-study at home, with periodic examinations by the school. If they pass, they can be exempted from a portion of their compulsory schooling.

(Note 5) Currently, there are a total of 1,915 counties in the country. If each county establishes one urban and one rural compulsory education experimental zone, there should be 1,915 of each of the aforementioned two types of experimental zones nationwide. However, impoverished counties can jointly establish one or two experimental zones in collaboration with two or more counties. Therefore, this plan only stipulates the establishment of approximately 1,500 urban and rural compulsory education experimental zones each nationwide within five years.

(Note 6) The former University Council had already prepared investigation forms in 1928 and issued them to the education administrative organs of various provinces and cities, requesting detailed reports on the number of school-age children. The original deadline for submission was the end of 1928. However, at that time, the Northern Expedition had just been successfully completed, and the military operations had not ended for long. Many provinces delayed the investigation of school-age children. As of September 1929, only Nanjing Special Municipality had submitted the exact number of school-age children to the ministry. The remaining provinces and cities did not provide accurate reports. Therefore, the number of school-age children nationwide can only be estimated based on the approximate population of the country. In European and American countries, approximately one in six people is a school-age child. However, the "school-age period" for Chinese children is tentatively set from six to twelve years old, which is shorter than in Europe and America. Furthermore, compulsory education is also tentatively aimed at "enabling all school-age children nationwide to receive four years of elementary school education." Therefore, the number can be further reduced. For now, it is tentatively assumed that one in ten people is a school-age child subject to compulsory education.

As the population census in various provinces and cities has not been completed, there are no accurate reports on the total population of the country. According to the estimate of the Statistics Bureau of the Beijing State Council before 1915, the national population was 377,673,424 people. The estimate of the Postal Administration in 1925 was 436,094,953 people. The estimate of the Customs Administration in 1928 was 448,231,000 people. After consulting various gazetteers, it is felt that the number estimated by the Postal Administration is more approximate.

If calculated based on a population of over 436 million, there are over 43.6 million school-age children nationwide. Excluding those who have already enrolled, there are still over 37.19 million children who do not have the opportunity to receive elementary education. To implement compulsory education, these over 37 million school-age children must be enrolled in school.

(Note 7) According to statistics before 1924, over 6.4 million school-age children nationwide have already enrolled in school. The number of enrollees may have increased now, but there are no accurate statistics to rely on. Therefore, this number is still used for deduction.

Assuming that 400,000 teachers retire in 20 years, then it will be sufficient to train 1.4 million teachers. According to the statistics of the China Education Improvement Society in 1925, there are a total of 195 normal schools nationwide, with a total of less than 10,000 graduates each year. There are also 106 normal school training courses and advanced courses, with a total of at most 5,000 graduates each year. To train over 1.4 million elementary school teachers in 20 years, a different approach is needed.

Based on the above table, each elementary school student requires over five yuan of public funds each year, each higher elementary school student requires over nineteen yuan of public funds each year, and each elementary vocational school student requires over thirty-one yuan of public funds each year. For now, it is tentatively defined that the expenses for four years of compulsory education only need to be calculated according to the elementary school standard. Before 1924, each elementary school student only required five yuan of public funds each year. However, since the various provinces and cities came under the rule of the National Government, the salaries of elementary school teachers have mostly been increased, and the facilities of elementary schools have also been improved compared to before. Therefore, the required amount of public funds should be increased. Based on the current situation, each elementary school student should require at least seven yuan of public funds each year. If 40 million children are to be universally enrolled in elementary school, then the government needs to increase compulsory education funding by 280 million yuan each year.

(Note 11) Currently, the public treasury is in financial difficulty, and it is feared that new classrooms cannot be specially built. We can only borrow civilian housing and repair it to ensure that the light and air in the rooms are suitable. It costs about 500 yuan to open a new class (including housing repair fees, school equipment purchase fees, and other administrative expenses). If the government has to bear 200 yuan to train a teacher, then it will cost 200 million yuan to train 1 million teachers, which is probably not enough in reality.

Chapter 2: Preliminary Plan for Implementing Adult Remedial Education

(1) Objectives

The objective of this plan is to provide a short-term, remedial school education to young people and adults nationwide who have dropped out of school. This remedial education is extremely important, but it does not occupy a fixed position in our country's education system. For convenience, it is simply called adult remedial education. Adult remedial education inherently includes both national literacy training and vocational training. This plan is a preliminary plan, and it aims to complete the major task of national literacy training as soon as possible within the six years of political tutelage. As for vocational training, it can refer to the vocational education sections in Chapter 5, the Plan to Improve Secondary Education, and Chapter 7, the Plan to Improve Social Education.

(2) Principles

A. National literacy training should use the least amount of money and the shortest amount of time to enable the general public to have the ability to read and write and exercise their four rights.

B. National literacy training should start with organized groups of people and gradually extend to scattered populations. It should start in affluent areas and gradually extend to impoverished areas. Except for areas with natural disasters or special circumstances, it should not be delayed.

C. The age of those receiving national literacy training should range from 12 to 50 years old.

D. In national literacy training, not only those who are illiterate must bear the obligation to learn, but those who are already literate must also bear the obligation to teach.

E. The implementation of national literacy training should have very strict assessment.

F. After establishing a foundation in national literacy training, there should be opportunities for continued progress.

(3) Urgent Issues at Present

A. How to enable all out-of-school people nationwide to attend school? The illiterate population nationwide accounts for about 80% of the total population (Note 1). If the national population is tentatively estimated at 436,094,953 people, then based on various relationships and special reasons (Note 2), the number of those who are literate, illiterate, and should receive remedial education can be analyzed as follows:

I. Approximately 20% are literate, totaling 87,218,990 people.

II. Approximately 80% are illiterate, totaling 348,875,962 people.

1. Approximately 13.33% are over 50 years old, totaling 58,131,457 people.

2. Approximately 10% are school-age children, totaling 43,609,495 people.

3. Approximately 10% are children under 6 years old, totaling 43,609,495 people.

4. Approximately 0.25% are disabled such as blind, deaf, or mute, and those with mental or neurological illnesses, totaling 1,090,237 people.

5. Approximately 46.42% should receive remedial education, totaling 202,435,277 people.

Based on this table, the literate and illiterate populations are analyzed in the following diagram. Observing the table and diagram above, we know that the number of people who should receive adult remedial education is over 202 million, accounting for nearly half of our country's total population. This is the total number of people we are targeting for adult remedial education. How to enable these illiterate people to become literate, read books and newspapers, and do arithmetic is the first thing that should be discussed.

B. How should the required teachers be trained? Running adult remedial education should proceed in parallel with the implementation of compulsory education, so there will be many opportunities for utilization. There will also be quite a few teachers who can be assisted. However, before compulsory education is fully popularized, every year there are many school-age children who drop out of school and secretly join the number of young people who are out of school as they get older. Therefore, even if all primary schools are also used as adult remedial education institutions and all primary school teachers are also adult remedial education teachers in the process of promoting compulsory education, it can only offset the number that increases each year at most. These 202.4 million out-of-school people require another source of teachers to solve the problem. Assuming that the national literacy training for the 202.4 million out-of-school people is completed in six years, an average of 33.74 million people must be trained each year. Each person receives four months of training, and training can be divided into three sessions within a year. Each session averages about 11.24 million people. Each teacher rotates to teach two classes, with an average of 50 people per class, meaning each teacher teaches an average of 100 people. Approximately 112,470 teachers are needed. Within six years, 12% of the teachers must be replaced (according to the estimate in Chapter 1, the Compulsory Education Plan, 2% are replaced each year). A total of approximately 135,000 teachers are needed. How should these huge numbers of teachers be selected and trained? (To be continued)

Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau Issues Order to Various Bookstores

Book Titles of Various Textbooks Being Edited Should Be Simple and Appropriate

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued an order to various bookstores yesterday, stating, "To enforce the matter, in accordance with Order No. 324 of the Ministry of Education, regarding the matters that should be marked on the covers of various textbooks, the Ministry has prescribed six measures for rectification and has ordered the deletion of general book titles such as 'New Era' and 'New Doctrine'."

"All bookstores are hereby ordered to comply with and rectify accordingly, without any delay. Later, the Shanghai Booksellers Association submitted a statement stating the difficulties in deleting the general book titles and requesting that they be given discretion to make changes. The Ministry rejected the request and reiterated the previous order, instructing all bookstores to comply without any delay. Now, the Shanghai Zhonghua Book Company has reported that canceling words such as 'New China' and 'New Primary School' will make the book titles of various bookstores easily confused, causing difficulties for buyers to distinguish them, and requested that the Ministry review and issue instructions for compliance."

"Also attached are two copies each of the cover samples of the 'New China Chinese Language Reader' and the 'New Primary School Chinese Language Reader' sent to the Ministry. The Ministry believes that the various textbooks published by various bookstores often have the same specific general title above the book title, forming a set. The titles are too complicated, and it is doubtful whether the editing has a complete plan and whether the content has a practical connection. Moreover, the quality of the teaching materials varies. Among the books in the same set, some have been approved by the Ministry, and some have not. Therefore, although the name is a set, it is mostly incomplete. The specific general title that makes up a set has long lost its effect. Therefore, we have repeatedly ordered the deletion of the name."

"Now, the bookstore has repeatedly submitted reports on the difficulties faced by the bookstore and buyers and has changed the 'New China Textbook' and 'New Primary School Textbook' to 'New China New Primary School', listing it at the top of the book title in one line, and changed 'Textbook' to 'Coursebook', such as 'New China [Something] Coursebook' and 'New Primary School [Something] Coursebook'. The names are simpler and easier to identify. The claim that it is easy to confuse among various bookstores and difficult for buyers to distinguish is not unreasonable in fact. Therefore, we will temporarily allow changes. The names 'New China Chinese Language Coursebook' and 'New Primary School Chinese Language Coursebook' submitted by the bookstore should be approved for adoption, but the book titles of textbooks in the future should be as simple and appropriate as possible. The various bookstores should submit them to the Ministry for approval at any time to ensure consistency."

"In addition to the instructions, we hereby issue another order instructing the bookstores to comply accordingly. This order."

There are more than 400 photos of famous librarians in China, short biographies of 300,000 words, and more than 30 group photos, which is a grand sight. The hardbound volume has been praised by the Ministry of Education, which has ordered the library departments of various provincial education departments and bureaus to instruct the libraries in their provinces and regions to purchase two copies for public viewing. It is heard that the book is specially priced at 1.25 yuan per copy for domestic libraries and educational circles, and postage stamps are accepted. Domestic and foreign orders are very enthusiastic. Shen Bao Education News

Special Issue No. 9 of the National Games

The Eighth Day of the National Games

Heavy rain yesterday… Rest day

Competitions continue today… Strive again

Closing ceremony tomorrow morning…

Yesterday's Games Suspended Due to Rain

Yesterday was the seventh day of the National Games. Thunder rumbled in the morning, and heavy rain poured down. All the sports fields became swamps. The Competition Section of the Games, considering that the fields were difficult to use, announced a one-day postponement. The athletes have been working hard and competing intensely for days since the opening ceremony, inevitably becoming physically and mentally exhausted. Taking this opportunity to recuperate will allow them to show their skills even better in the finals.

Closing Ceremony Rescheduled

Scheduled for 9:00 AM on the 10th

Undetermined Championships Will Be Awarded Later

The closing ceremony of the Games was originally scheduled to be held at the track and field stadium at 1:00 PM on the 10th, as the rostrum was equipped with wireless telephone broadcasting for convenience. However, due to the heavy rain yesterday morning and the one-day suspension, the competitions had to be postponed until 5:00 or 6:00 PM on the 10th to be completed. President Dai Jitao and Vice President Zhang Jingjiang were also in urgent need of returning to the capital for official business on the afternoon of the 10th. Therefore, they discussed with Directors Zhu and Zhou yesterday afternoon and decided to hold the closing ceremony at 9:00 AM on the 10th. No matter what, it cannot be postponed. The prizes for the determined women's track and field, men's track and field, all-around, and baseball championships will be awarded first. The undetermined championships for men's basketball, volleyball, soccer, tennis, and swimming will be awarded the next day. The prizes for the overall championship will also be postponed for two days.

Protecting Referees

Armed Police Protection Starts Today

After the Liaoning vs. Nanjing soccer game the day before yesterday, the referee Huang Wenjian was beaten and injured. Currently, all referees are fearful of serving the Games. To protect human rights and maintain the prestige and safety of the referees, the Games will deploy armed police protection for the referees of all ball games starting today. If such an unfortunate incident occurs again, the police will be made to suffer disgrace rather than allowing the referees to be endangered.

The Games Hosted a Farewell for He Yingqin Yesterday

He Yingqin, Vice President of the National Games, arrived in Hangzhou on the 5th and went to the Games to observe the competitions. He was deeply satisfied with the spirit of the athletes and the layout of the venue. He took a train to Shanghai at 5:30 PM on the 8th. President Dai Jitao and Zhang Jingjiang, Chen Bulei, Zhou Xiangxian, Ma Xun, and over a hundred members of the military band went to the station to bid him farewell. He was extremely happy when he left.

### Baseball Championship

Tianjin and Hong Kong to Compete Today

Previous Competition Overview

Baseball has historically lacked promotion in our country. Consequently, the number of teams participating in the Games is smaller compared to other sports. Seven teams, including Hunan, Shanghai, Tianjin, Hubei, Jiangxi, Beiping, and Hong Kong, registered. In the actual competition, only Hunan, Shanghai, Tianjin, and Hong Kong started the first round. Shanghai defeated Hunan with a score of 11-0. Subsequently, Shanghai competed against Tianjin, initially holding a 1-0 lead for the first six innings. However, their efforts fell short, and Tianjin, in a desperate situation, surpassed them, ultimately securing the final qualification with a score of 4-1. Tianjin's victory was attributed to their powerful hitting, with each player displaying exceptional agility and prowess. Additionally, Shanghai committed two significant errors, leading to Tianjin's ultimate success. Hong Kong boasts many talented players and is considered a strong contender for the championship. The area is seen as having superior talent and the victory is anticipated. The ultimate outcome of the championship will depend on the efforts of the Tianjin and Hong Kong teams today.

Swimming competition entry into the water scene, Photography: Wang Kaishe

Swimming Championship

Hong Kong Team Likely to Win the Championship

Liaoning, Guangdong, and Shanghai to Compete for Second Place

The results of the first day of the swimming competition preliminaries showed that the Liaoning team was a surprising success. Shi Xinglong won the one-mile freestyle with excellent results. Hong Kong secured the second and fourth positions respectively, while Guangdong came in third. The Shanghai team did not qualify. However, the Liaoning team has too few members, making their championship hopes slim. Hong Kong has a wealth of talent. Judging from the preliminary results, they can steadily secure first place in the point standings. The remaining unaired events include the 220-yard breaststroke and the 160-yard medley relay. With Hong Kong's average talent, the championship in the 160-yard race is assured. Therefore, the swimming championship is likely to go to Hong Kong.

### Shi Xinglong's Swimming Posture, Photography: Lin Zeren

Guangdong is likely to win the 100-yard backstroke. Although Yu Binqi from Shanghai secured first place in the third group, the results are significantly different, making their hopes slim, but they can certainly secure a position. The remaining three events will be more difficult to score points in. Therefore, although the Liaoning, Guangdong, and Shanghai teams will compete for second place, Liaoning and Guangdong have better chances. Let's predict the scores of each team and compare them with the final results.
